&lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt; &lt;div style=&#34;-moz-user-select: none; -webkit-user-select: none; -ms-user-select:none; user-select:none;-o-user-select:none;&#34; unselectable=&#34;on&#34; onselectstart=&#34;return false;&#34; onmousedown=&#34;return false;&#34;&gt; &lt;p&gt;A CPU scheduler executes processes in time quantum of 100ms and then calculates the next process to execute after each quantum.&lt;br/&gt; 3 processes are fed into our CPU&#39;s process scheduler with the following attributes&lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;Process A&lt;br/&gt; Arrival Time: 0 msec&lt;br/&gt; Execution Time Needed: 1900 msec&lt;/p&gt; &lt;br/&gt; &lt;p&gt;Process B&lt;br/&gt; Arrival Time: 800 msec&lt;br/&gt; Execution Time Needed: 1100 msec&lt;/p&gt; &lt;br/&gt; &lt;p&gt;Process C&lt;br/&gt; Arrival Time: 900 msec&lt;br/&gt; Execution Time Needed: 900 msec&lt;/p&gt; &lt;br/&gt; &lt;p&gt;There are four main algorithms which our CPU uses to schedule processes:&lt;br/&gt; FCFR: First Come First Serve&lt;br/&gt; SJF: Shortest Job First&lt;br/&gt; SRTF: Shortest Remaining Time First&lt;br/&gt; RR: Round Robin&lt;/p&gt; &lt;br/&gt; &lt;p&gt;If the scheduler is using the FCFR algorithm to schedule processes, which processes would have been completed after 2500 ms?&lt;/p&gt; &lt;/div&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;wrapper-problem-response&#34; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt; &lt;p&gt;&lt;i&gt;An array is used here to represent a Hash Table. Array index starts from &lt;b&gt;0&lt;/b&gt; and ends at &lt;b&gt;size_of_array - 1&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br/&gt; Which slot would the number 23 hash to, in the following Hash Table? &lt;br/&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt; &lt;p&gt; Given the following processes with their arrival and burst time given below, calculate the average waiting time using the &lt;u&gt;First Come First Serve&lt;/u&gt; approach. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; &lt;b&gt;Arrival time&lt;/b&gt;: Time when the process is ready for its execution on the CPU. &lt;br/&gt; &lt;b&gt;Burst time&lt;/b&gt;: Time required by the process to complete its execution on the CPU. &lt;br/&gt; &lt;b&gt;Waiting time&lt;/b&gt;: Time spent by the process waiting for the CPU after its arrival. &lt;br/&gt; &lt;/p&gt; &lt;table style=&#34;width:100%; text-align: left;&#34;&gt; &lt;tr&gt; &lt;th&gt;Process&lt;/th&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt; &lt;p&gt;There are two storage systems present, one is a stack and the other queue. The content of the stack is &lt;strong&gt;[7, 14, 5, 11]&lt;/strong&gt; and the content of the queue is &lt;strong&gt;[19, 17, 18, 27, 26, 28, 15, 24, 22, 25]&lt;/strong&gt; (the first item in both represent the first item stored). The number on each item represent the ID of item. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt;We have to balance these storage systems (move items between storages so that there are equal number of items in both). Keeping in mind the functionalities of stacks and queues, we have to balance them! &lt;/p&gt; &lt;pre&gt; &lt;h3&gt;STACK STORAGE: &lt;i&gt;oldest&lt;/i&gt; &lt;strong&gt; [7, 14, 5, 11] &lt;/strong&gt; &lt;div class=&#34;problem&#34;&gt; &lt;div&gt; &lt;p&gt; Each row below are the stacks of water bottles with their respective heights(n) &lt;h2&gt;&lt;b&gt; 1. | 2 | 2 | 1 | 1 | 4 | 4 | &lt;/b&gt;&lt;/h2&gt; &lt;h2&gt;&lt;b&gt; 2. | 5 | 1 | 3 | 1 | 4 | 3 | 4 | 4 | &lt;/b&gt;&lt;/h2&gt; &lt;h2&gt;&lt;b&gt; 3. | 2 | 4 | 1 | 5 | &lt;/b&gt;&lt;/h2&gt; The rightmost element shows the top of the stack. Adding up the heights of the bottles on a stack will give you the overall height of the stack. You can pop the bottles from each stack any number of times to change the height of the stack. &lt;/p&gt; &lt;p&gt; Determine the maximum height of each stack where all of the three stacks are equal in terms of height.&lt;/p&gt; Questions

Process Scheduling

1 point possible (graded, results hidden)

A CPU scheduler executes processes in time quantum of 100ms and then calculates the next process to execute after each quantum.
3 processes are fed into our CPU's process scheduler with the following attributes

Process A
Arrival Time: 0 msec
Execution Time Needed: 1900 msec


Process B
Arrival Time: 800 msec
Execution Time Needed: 1100 msec


Process C
Arrival Time: 900 msec
Execution Time Needed: 900 msec


There are four main algorithms which our CPU uses to schedule processes:
FCFR: First Come First Serve
SJF: Shortest Job First
SRTF: Shortest Remaining Time First
RR: Round Robin


If the scheduler is using the FCFR algorithm to schedule processes, which processes would have been completed after 2500 ms?

submitted
Some problems have options such as save, reset, hints, or show answer. These options follow the Submit button.
Answer submitted.
None
Answers are displayed within the problem

Hash Clash

1 point possible (graded, results hidden)

An array is used here to represent a Hash Table. Array index starts from 0 and ends at size_of_array - 1
Which slot would the number 23 hash to, in the following Hash Table?

-- 23 41 -- -- -- 40 42 29 -- --

size_of_table = 11

The hash function is :

hash(number):number % size_of_table

For collision resolution use the following rehash function:

new_hash_value:rehash(old_hash_value)
rehash(position):(position+1) % size_of_table

Algorithm

1 point possible (graded, results hidden)

What is the output of the following code?


func min_jumps(arr[], start, end)
{
    if(start == end)
        return 0;

    int min = INT_MAX;  // Max value of int

    for(idx = 1; arr[start] >= idx AND end >= start + idx; idx++)
    {
        int jumps = min_jumps(arr, start + idx, end) + 1;
        if(min > jumps)
            min = jumps;
    }
    return min;
}

main()
{
    arr[] = [1, 1, 1, 3, 4, 1, 1, 1, 4, 1],
    ans = min_jumps(arr, 0, lenOfArr);
    print ans;

class Class1:
    function function_1(self):
         print("a")

    function function_2(self):
         print("b")


class Class2:
    function function_1(self):
         print("c")

    function function_3(self):
         print("d")


class Class3:
    function function_2(self):
         print("e")

    function function_3(self):
         print("f")


class ClassA(Class3, Class1):
    function function_3(self):
         print("h")


class ClassB(Class2):
    function function_2(self):
         print("i")

    function function_3(self):
         print("j")


class ClassC(Class1):
    function function_2(self):
         print("k")

    function function_3(self):
         print("l")

Round and Round

1 point possible (graded, results hidden)

We have come upon a 'longRunning' method in our code. In order to check its lengthy execution time, we are calculating its iterations against different inputs.

Can you figure out the number of iterations it will take to execute the following input:

[6, 14, 16, 16, 20] 

      
function longRunningFunction(array) {
  for ( i = 0; i < length(array); i++ ) {
    idx = i
    for ( j = i + 1; j < length(array); j++ ) {
      if ( array[idx] > array[j] ) {
        idx = j
      }
    }
    swap( array[i], array[idx] )
  }
}

Travelkitties

1 point possible (graded, results hidden)

Travelkitties is a travel aggregator which allow users to book recreational trips using their app from all arround the world. You've been given a task to find out top 1 travel desitination (city) to help business team in making data driven decisions.
Note: Travel desitination is arriving city of trip.

user
uid name age
1 Joe Williams 59
2 John Smith 58
3 Andy Smith 22
4 Andy Williams 23
5 John Johnson 54
city
cid lat lng city country_code
1 34.95303 -120.43572 Austin US
2 42.16808 -88.42814 Los Angeles US
3 39.96097 -75.60804 Seattle US
4 34.09668 -117.71978 New York US
5 46.09273 -88.64235 Dallas US
trips
tid uid origin_id destination_id
1 3 3 2
2 2 1 2
3 2 1 2
4 4 5 2
5 1 1 3
6 5 4 4
7 2 4 5

With given tables what would be output of following SQL query:


SELECT
  city_name
FROM (
  SELECT
        city AS city_name,
                    count(t.destination_id) AS trips
  FROM city AS c
  INNER JOIN trips AS t
  ON c.cid = t.destination_id
  GROUP BY city, t.destination_id
) AS ranked_trips
ORDER BY trips DESC
LIMIT 1;
